<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" border="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-weight:bold;border-collapse:collapse;text-align:left;width:100%;font-size:10pt;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;border:0;">
<tr style="page-break-inside:avoid;">
<td style="width:10%;vertical-align:top;white-space:nowrap;">Item&#160;2.02. </td>
<td style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-weight:bold;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;">Results of Operation and Financial Condition.</td> </tr> </table> <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;text-align:left;text-indent:4%;font-size:10pt;margin-bottom:0px;margin-top:6pt">On February&#160;3, 2020, ON Semiconductor Corporation (the &#8220;Company&#8221;) announced in a news release its financial performance for the fourth quarter and year ended December&#160;31, 2019 and other related material information (the &#8220;Earnings Release&#8221;). A copy of the Earnings Release is attached hereto as Exhibit 99.1 and incorporated herein by reference. </p> <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;text-align:left;text-indent:4%;font-size:10pt;margin-bottom:0px;margin-top:12pt">The information in Item&#160;2.02 of this report, including Exhibit 99.1, is being furnished under Item&#160;2.02 and shall not be deemed to be &#8220;filed&#8221; for purposes of Section&#160;18 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the &#8220;Exchange Act&#8221;), or otherwise subject to liability under that section nor shall such information be deemed incorporated by reference in any filing under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, or the Exchange Act, regardless of any general incorporation language in such filing, except as shall be expressly set forth by specific reference in such filing. </p> <p style="margin-bottom:0px;margin-top:18pt"></p>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="justify" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Operating cash flow of $694.7&nbsp;million and free cash flow of $160.1&nbsp;million </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="10%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="justify" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">GAAP diluted earnings per share of $0.51 and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted earnings
per share of $1.49 </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify"><B>PHOENIX, Ariz. &#150; Feb. 3, 2020 &#150;</B> ON Semiconductor Corporation (Nasdaq: ON) today
announced that total revenue in the fourth quarter of 2019 was $1,401.8&nbsp;million, down approximately 7&nbsp;percent compared to the same quarter last year. Fourth quarter revenue was up approximately 1&nbsp;percent as compared to revenue in the
third quarter of 2019. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">&#147;Our performance in 2019 validates the transforming nature of our business, as we expect to outperform most
of our peer group against a backdrop of challenging macroeconomic and geopolitical conditions. We believe that our strong competitive position in automotive, industrial, and cloud-power semiconductor
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">end-markets,</FONT> and exposure to secular trends in these markets continue to be the key drivers of our superior performance,&#148; said Keith Jackson, president and CEO of ON Semiconductor. &#147;Along with strong
revenue performance, we are taking substantial measures to expand our margins by making structural changes to our manufacturing footprint, and accelerating the timeline for production at our 300mm fab.&#148; </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">&#147;In the fourth quarter, we saw moderate improvement in business trends, and the improvement has continued thus far in the first quarter
of 2020. With improving macroeconomic and geopolitical conditions, solid product portfolio with exposure to the most attractive semiconductor <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">end-markets,</FONT> and ongoing structural improvements to our cost
structure, ON Semiconductor is well positioned to deliver strong near to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-term</FONT> performance.&#148; </P>
</DIV></Center>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>FIRST QUARTER 2020 OUTLOOK </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Based on product booking trends, backlog levels, and estimated turns levels, the Company anticipates that first quarter of 2020 revenue will be
approximately $1,355 to $1,405&nbsp;million. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> gross margin for first quarter
2020 is expected to be between 33.7&nbsp;percent and 34.7&nbsp;percent. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The outlook for the first quarter of 2020 includes anticipated
stock-based compensation expense of approximately $19&nbsp;million to $21&nbsp;million. Net cash paid for income taxes is expected to be $14&nbsp;million to $18&nbsp;million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The following table outlines ON Semiconductor&#146;s projected first quarter of 2020 GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT>
outlook. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">**</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Diluted share count can vary as a result of, among other things, the actual exercise of options or vesting of
restricted stock units, the incremental dilutive shares from the Company&#146;s convertible senior subordinated notes, and the repurchase or the issuance of stock or convertible notes or the sale of treasury shares. In periods in which the quarterly
average stock price per share exceeds $18.50, the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share count and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> net income per share includes the impact of the Company&#146;s hedge
transactions issued concurrently with our 1.00% convertible notes. As such, at an average stock price per share between $18.50 and $25.96, the hedging activity offsets the potentially dilutive effect of the 1.00% convertible notes. In periods when
the quarterly average stock price per share exceeds $20.72, the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share count and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> net income per share includes the anti-dilutive impact of the
Company&#146;s hedge transactions issued concurrently with the 1.625% convertible notes. As such, at an average stock price per share between $20.72 and $30.70, the hedging activity offsets the potentially dilutive effect of the 1.625% convertible
notes. Both GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share counts are based on the Company&#146;s stock price as of December&nbsp;31, 2019. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">***</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Special items may include: amortization of acquisition-related intangibles; expensing of appraised inventory
fair market value <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">step-up;</FONT> purchased <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-process</FONT> research and development expenses; restructuring, asset impairments and other, net; goodwill impairment charges; gains
and losses on debt prepayment; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> interest expense; actuarial (gains) losses on pension plans and other pension benefits; and certain other special items, as necessary. These special items are out of our
control and could change significantly from period to period. As a result, we are not able to reasonably estimate and separately present the individual impact of these special items, and we are similarly unable to provide a reconciliation of the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures. The reconciliation that is unavailable would include a forward looking income statement, balance sheet and statement of cash flows in accordance with GAAP.&nbsp;For this reason, we use a projected
range of the aggregate amount of special items in order to calculate our projected <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating expense outlook. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">****</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">We believe these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures provide important supplemental
information to investors. We use these measures, together with GAAP measures, for internal managerial purposes and as a means to evaluate <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">period-to-period</FONT></FONT> comparisons.
However, we do not, and you should not, rely on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures alone as measures of our performance. We believe that <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures reflect an
additional way of viewing aspects of our operations that, when taken together with GAAP results and the reconciliations to corresponding GAAP financial measures that we also provide in our releases, provide a more complete understanding of factors
and trends affecting our business. Because <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures are not standardized, it may not be possible to compare these financial measures with other companies&#146;
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures, even if they have similar names. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>TELECONFERENCE </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">ON Semiconductor will host a conference call for the financial community at 9 a.m. Eastern Time (EST) on Feb. 3, 2020 to discuss this
announcement and ON Semiconductor&#146;s results for the fourth quarter of 2019 and year then ended. The Company will also provide a real-time audio webcast of the teleconference on the Investor Relations page of its website at
http://www.onsemi.com. The webcast replay will be available at this site approximately one hour following the live broadcast and will continue to be available for approximately 30 days following the conference call. Investors and interested parties
can also access the conference call through a telephone call by dialing (877) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">356-3762</FONT> (U.S./Canada) or (262) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">558-6155</FONT> (International).&nbsp;In order to join this
conference call, you will be required to provide the Conference ID Number, which is 9592878.</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About ON Semiconductor </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">ON Semiconductor (Nasdaq: ON) is driving energy efficient innovations, empowering customers to reduce global energy use. The Company is a
leading supplier of semiconductor-based solutions, offering a comprehensive portfolio of energy efficient power management, analog, sensors, logic, timing, connectivity, discrete, SoC and custom devices. The Company&#146;s products help engineers
solve their unique design challenges in automotive, communications, computing, consumer, industrial, medical, aerospace and defense applications. ON Semiconductor operates a responsive, reliable, world-class supply chain and quality program, a
robust compliance and ethics program and a network of manufacturing facilities, sales offices and design centers in key markets throughout North America, Europe and the Asia Pacific regions. For more information, visit <U>http://www.onsemi.com</U>.
</P>

significant business, including Hong Kong, as well as <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">man-made</FONT> and/or natural disasters affecting our operations or financial results; the threat or occurrence of international armed conflict and terrorist
activities both in the United States and internationally; risks of changes in U.S. or international tax rates or legislation; risks related to the potential impact of climate change and regulations related thereto on our operations; risks and costs
associated with increased and new regulation of corporate governance and disclosure standards; risks related to new legal requirements; and risks and expenses involving environmental or other governmental regulation. Additional factors that could
affect our future results or events are described under Part I, Item 1A &#147;Risk Factors&#148; in our 2018 Annual Report on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> filed with the SEC on February&nbsp;20, 2019 (our &#147;2018 Form <FONT

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> MEASURES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">To supplement the consolidated financial results prepared in accordance with GAAP, ON Semiconductor uses
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">certain&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;measures,</FONT> which are adjusted from the most directly comparable GAAP measures to exclude items related to the amortization of intangible assets, amortization of acquisition-related
intangibles, expensing of appraised inventory fair market <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">value&nbsp;step-up,&nbsp;inventory</FONT> valuation adjustments, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">purchased&nbsp;in-process</FONT> research and development
expenses, restructuring, asset impairments and other, net, goodwill impairment charges, gains and losses on debt <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">prepayment,&nbsp;non-cash&nbsp;interest</FONT> expense, actuarial (gains) losses on pension plans and
other pension benefits, third party acquisition and divestiture related costs, tax impact of these items, and certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">other&nbsp;non-recurring&nbsp;items,</FONT> as necessary. Management does not consider the effects
of these items in evaluating the core operational activities of ON Semiconductor. Management uses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">these&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;measures</FONT> internally to make strategic decisions, forecast future results, and evaluate
ON Semiconductor&#146;s current performance. In addition, we believe that most analysts covering ON Semiconductor use <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">the&nbsp;non-GAAP</FONT> measures to evaluate ON Semiconductor&#146;s performance. Given
management&#146;s and other relevant use of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">these&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;measures,</FONT> ON Semiconductor believes these measures are important to investors in understanding ON Semiconductor&#146;s current and future
operating results as seen through the eyes of management. In addition, management believes <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">these&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;measures</FONT> are useful to investors in enabling them to better assess changes in ON
Semiconductor&#146;s core business across different time periods. <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">These&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;measures</FONT> are not prepared in accordance with, and should not be considered alternatives or necessarily superior to,
GAAP financial data and may be different <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">from&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;measures</FONT> used by other companies. <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Because&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measures are not standardized, it
may not be possible to compare these financial measures with other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">companies&#146;&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measures, even if they have similar names. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Adjusted EBITDA </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">Adjusted EBITDA is <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">a&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measure that represents net income before interest expense, interest income, provision for income taxes, depreciation, and amortization expense and special items. We use the adjusted
EBITDA measure for internal managerial evaluation purposes, as a means to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">evaluate&nbsp;period-to-period&nbsp;comparisons</FONT></FONT> and as a performance metric for the vesting and
release of certain of our performance-based equity awards. SEC Regulation G and other federal securities laws regulate the use of financial measures that are not prepared in accordance with GAAP. We believe this measure provides important
supplemental information to investors. However, we do not, and you should not, rely <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">on&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measures alone as measures of our performance. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP&nbsp;Gross</FONT> Profit and Gross Margin </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;gross</FONT> profit and gross margin allows management to evaluate, among other
things, the gross margin and gross profit of the Company&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-cash&nbsp;items</FONT> including, generally
speaking, expensing of appraised inventory fair market <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">value&nbsp;step-up&nbsp;and</FONT> the impact from the change in revenue recognition on distributor sales. In addition, it is an important component of
management&#146;s internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets, and
forecasting future results. Management presents <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">this&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measure to enable investors and analysts to evaluate our revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of revenue
of ON Semiconductor&#146;s core businesses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP&nbsp;Operating</FONT> Income and&nbsp;Operating Margin </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;operating</FONT> income and operating margin allows management to evaluate,
among other things, the operating margin and operating income of the Company&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-cash&nbsp;items</FONT>
including, generally speaking, expensing of appraised inventory fair market <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">value&nbsp;step-up,&nbsp;the</FONT> impact from the change in revenue recognition on distributor sales, amortization and impairments of
intangible assets, third party acquisition and divestiture related costs, restructuring charges, and certain other special items as necessary. In addition, it is an important component of management&#146;s internal performance measurement and
incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets, and forecasting future results. Management presents <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">this&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measure to enable investors and analysts to evaluate our revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of operations of ON Semiconductor&#146;s core businesses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP&nbsp;Net</FONT> Income Attributable to ON Semiconductor and Diluted Earnings Per Share </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;net</FONT> income attributable to ON Semiconductor and diluted earnings per
share allows management to evaluate the operating results of ON Semiconductor&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-cash&nbsp;items</FONT>
including, generally, the amortization and impairments of intangible assets, expensing of appraised inventory fair market <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">value&nbsp;step-up,&nbsp;the</FONT> impact from the change in revenue recognition on
distributor sales, restructuring, gains and losses on debt <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">prepayment,&nbsp;non-cash&nbsp;interest</FONT> expense, actuarial (gains) losses on pension plans and other pension benefits, third party acquisition and
divestiture related costs, tax impact of these items and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">other&nbsp;non-GAAP</FONT> adjustments, </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">16 </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> MEASURES (Continued) </B></P>
<p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">
and certain other special items, as necessary. In addition, these items are important components of management&#146;s internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process, as they
are used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, setting targets, and forecasting future results. Management presents
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">these&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measures to enable investors and analysts to understand the results of operations of ON Semiconductor&#146;s core businesses and, to the extent comparable, to compare our
results of operations on a more consistent basis against that of other companies in our industry. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Free Cash Flow </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of free cash flow allows management to evaluate, among other things, the ability of the Company to make interest or principal payments
on its debt. Free cash flow is defined as the difference between cash flow from operating activities and capital expenditures disclosed under investing activities in the consolidated statement of cash flows. Free cash flow is not an alternate to
cash flow from operating activities as a measure of liquidity. It is an important component of management&#146;s internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results
of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets, and forecasting future results. Management presents <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">this&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;financial</FONT> measure to enable investors and
analysts to evaluate our revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of operations of ON Semiconductor&#146;s core businesses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Diluted
Share Count </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">In periods when the quarterly average stock price per share exceeds $18.50,
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">the&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;diluted</FONT> share count includes the anti-dilutive impact of the Company&#146;s hedge transactions issued concurrently with the 1.00% convertible notes. As such, at an average stock price
per share between $18.50 and $25.96, the hedging activity offsets the potentially dilutive effect of the 1.00% convertible notes. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">In
periods when the quarterly average stock price per share exceeds $20.72, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">the&nbsp;non-GAAP&nbsp;diluted</FONT> share count includes the anti-dilutive impact of the Company&#146;s hedge transactions issued
concurrently with the 1.625% convertible notes. As such, at an average stock price per share between $20.72 and $30.70, the hedging activity offsets the potentially dilutive effect of the 1.625% convertible notes. Management presents this <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measure to enable investors and analysts to compare our results of operations on a more consistent basis against that of other companies in our industry. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">17 </P>

</DIV></Center>
